  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_381a266f-1cbc-400b-acc5-d0d824687544'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11809613168969359737">Over and again, the aged seeress Tamis scried all the possible tomorrows. In every one, dark forces threatened Greece; terrible evil was poised to reenter the world. The future held only one hope: a half-caste Spartan boy, Parmenion. So Tamis made it her mission to see that Parmenion would before the deadliest warrior in the world -- no matter what the cost.<br/><br/>Raised to manho</span>
  <span id="freeText11809613168969359737" style="display:none">Over and again, the aged seeress Tamis scried all the possible tomorrows. In every one, dark forces threatened Greece; terrible evil was poised to reenter the world. The future held only one hope: a half-caste Spartan boy, Parmenion. So Tamis made it her mission to see that Parmenion would before the deadliest warrior in the world -- no matter what the cost.<br /><br />Raised to manhood in Sparta, bullied and forced to fight for his life every day, Parmenion had no notion of the unseen dimensions of magic and mystery that shaped his fate. He grew in strength and cunning. His military genius earned him the title Strategos in Sparta. His triumphs for the city of Thebes made him a hero. And finally his fate led him to the service of Philip of Macedon.<br /><br />As Tamis had foreseen, Parmenion's destiny was tied to the Dark God, to Philip, and to the yet-unborn Alexander. All too soon the future was upon them. Parmenion stood poised to defeat evil -- or to open the gate for the Dark God to reenter the world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11809613168969359737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4488679067681490284">Lion of Macedon (Greek Series, #1), David Gemmell<br/>Lion of Macedon is a historic fantasy novel by English author David Gemmell. First published in 1990, it and its 1991 sequel, Dark Prince, follow the career of a fictionalized version of the Macedonian general Parmenion. The story is loosely based on historic events, but adds fantasy elements such as supernatural creatures and sorcery that become even more significant in the book's sequel, Dark Prince. <br/>As the story opens, Tamis, a sorceress, is se</span>
  <span id="freeText4488679067681490284" style="display:none">Lion of Macedon (Greek Series, #1), David Gemmell<br />Lion of Macedon is a historic fantasy novel by English author David Gemmell. First published in 1990, it and its 1991 sequel, Dark Prince, follow the career of a fictionalized version of the Macedonian general Parmenion. The story is loosely based on historic events, but adds fantasy elements such as supernatural creatures and sorcery that become even more significant in the book's sequel, Dark Prince. <br />As the story opens, Tamis, a sorceress, is seeing the future. She discovers that only a mixed-blood Spartan called Parmenion can help her. Parmenion is a half-blood Spartan (a Mothax) whose mother is from Macedon. He is an accomplished runner and a strategic genius, yet he is despised by the young Spartan nobles for being a half-blood. He is forced to kill a love rival in duel and then flees to Thebes. ...<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سیزدهم ماه می سال 2012 میلادی<br />عنوان: شیر مقدونیه؛ نویسنده: دیوید گمل؛ کترجم: طاهره صدیقیان؛ تهران، کتابسرای تندیس؛ 1389؛ در 567 ص؛ شابک: 9789648944549؛ موضوع: داستان پارمینیون از سال 400 پیش از میلاد تا 330 پیش از میلاد<br />شیر مقدونیه یا ژنرال پارمینیون رزم‌آرا، قهرمانی تنها که در جستجوی رستگاری ست، سرنوشتش این است که رزم آرای سپاه فلیپ دوم پدر اسکندر و سپس فرمانده ارشد و رزم آرای لشگر اسکندر شود. و ... ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5306597217118871158">This book markets itself as historical fantasy but really it's a historical fiction with some supernatural elements. Hence my first disappointment. I was also underwhelmed by the characters who were all fairly bland and predictable. Then there was the plot, which consisted of endless descriptions of military manoeuvres and battle formations, all of which went completely over my head (and most people's heads I would assume) and made me wonder why the author felt the need to include this tedious d</span>
  <span id="freeText5306597217118871158" style="display:none">This book markets itself as historical fantasy but really it's a historical fiction with some supernatural elements. Hence my first disappointment. I was also underwhelmed by the characters who were all fairly bland and predictable. Then there was the plot, which consisted of endless descriptions of military manoeuvres and battle formations, all of which went completely over my head (and most people's heads I would assume) and made me wonder why the author felt the need to include this tedious description in what he clearly hoped would be a mainstream novel. Then, of course, no mediocre historical/supernatural novel would be complete without the clash of the Good and Bad forces. I have no intention of completing the series but I'll hazard a guess and say Good wins. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18810398-andy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18810398-andy?shelf=hist-f-ancient">hist-f-ancient</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938306390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6184617118874311367">After enjoying the author’s Troy trilogy I really wanted to pick up another series of his in the same vein & so I plumped for the Greek series......<br/><br/>The story revolves around Parmenion, a Spartan “outcast” for want of a better word & his building hatred of Sparta as they reject him for no other reason than not being pure-blood, his mother a Macedonian.... He rises as a mercenary to become a Strategos (general) & we follow him around the Greek City states & historically I learnt a lot about Sparta</span>
  <span id="freeText6184617118874311367" style="display:none">After enjoying the author’s Troy trilogy I really wanted to pick up another series of his in the same vein &amp; so I plumped for the Greek series......<br /><br />The story revolves around Parmenion, a Spartan “outcast” for want of a better word &amp; his building hatred of Sparta as they reject him for no other reason than not being pure-blood, his mother a Macedonian.... He rises as a mercenary to become a Strategos (general) &amp; we follow him around the Greek City states &amp; historically I learnt a lot about Sparta &amp; its strife/hatred/envy within the Greek states &amp; then later how Thebes rose to power &amp; in turn Macedon became the foremost power in Greece through Philip of Macedon. Enjoyed this very much &amp; a very readable 5 stars.<br /><br />The writing is much in the same vein as his Troy Trilogy which was grand &amp; I'm onto a winner.....<br /><br />However...... Some of the fantasy elements (which aren't present in the Troy trilogy) are a little daft tbh, like Aristotle being a Magi who can walk through solid rock...... they allow the story a few get out of jail cards. The main fantasy element revolves around seers &amp; in a mythological sense it fits well enough into the story &amp; you let it ride with you...... BUT..... the last 50 pages is pure fantasy &amp; despite a lot of Oh yeah.... thats sound enough moments it did get (obviously) a little far fetched at times &amp; so overall I give the book a 4 stars rating.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1963630873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963630873" />
    <a title="Kostas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas"><img alt="Kostas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554812738p2/25638423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1963630873?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kostas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kostas" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas">Kostas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781857236224" href="/book/show/1061687.Lion_of_Macedon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=heroic-fantasy">heroic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1963630873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17461136774348902090">8.5/10<br/><br/>Back in the early ‘90s, when his career was still growing at the time, David Gemmell, taking a trip to Lindos, on the island of Rhodes, and an experience that proved more inspiring than he expected, started building his first ideas for his next story, bringing back to life from the depths of the Greek history a long-forgotten legend: Parmenion.<br/>And in the <i>Lion of Macedon</i>, the first of the two installments of the Greek series, Gemmell, based on true events as written in history, creates thro</span>
  <span id="freeText17461136774348902090" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />Back in the early ‘90s, when his career was still growing at the time, David Gemmell, taking a trip to Lindos, on the island of Rhodes, and an experience that proved more inspiring than he expected, started building his first ideas for his next story, bringing back to life from the depths of the Greek history a long-forgotten legend: Parmenion.<br />And in the <i>Lion of Macedon</i>, the first of the two installments of the Greek series, Gemmell, based on true events as written in history, creates through his imagination his own world of the ancient times, traveling us in a story of mercenaries and generals, philosophers and orators, and seeresses and priestesses, but also in an adventure of love and glory, vengeance and war, and destiny and magic, in an epic, historical fantasy novel.<br /><br />For almost a century since Xerxes’s great invasion, when the legendary Sword King Leonidas and his three hundred men stood at the Pass of Thermopylae, and when not long after five thousand united Spartans met the Persian army forcing it to flee from their lands, Sparta, a place where heroes and great warriors are born, has become the most militarily mighty and glorious city, spreading its dominance across Greece – but Parmenion, having been taken from his Macedonian mother at his seventh years of age to be trained to the ways of the warriors, falling victim to the mockings and tauntings of the other kids for his mix-blood parentage, has been dreaming all his young life for the day he will feel the glory of victory at the side of the King.<br />Wanting to prove himself worthy of his father’s side, and to make his mother proud for the sacrifices she underwent to raise him after his death, hoping to bring her some joy, Parmenion has been exercising hard day by day, surpassing his rivals in the running competitions, and bringing him closer than anyone else in his barracks at the Final of the General’s Games and the biggest prize that any Spartan could have: one of the seven swords of Leonidas the King.<br />Yet, with his mix-blood parentage to have caused the King Agesilau’s objection at competing in the Final, manipulating the judges in favor of his nephew, when his carefully prepared strategies lead to an overwhelming outcome like no one else has achieved ever before, and he falls in love with a girl who had been promised for someone else, Parmenion will soon find himself in the noble families’ target, seeking restoration for the shame and humiliation that he brought them, and putting him on a path that will deprive him all that he loved and cared about in this city.<br /><br />Meanwhile, in Thebes, Epaminondas, having felt the burden of the Spartan hegemony after the occupation of the Cadmea by their troops, seeing his people fall into daily suffering, has been plotting and planning ever since along with Calepios and Pelopidas, seeking for a way to liberate the city that they grew up and loved; Philip, having been given as a hostage after his father’s murder, and the seizing of the throne by his uncle, Ptolemaos, awaits for the day that he and his brother, Perdiccas, will take back Macedonia and their heritage and bring it again to glory; while Tamis, having walked the paths of the past and the future, seeing the birth of the Dark God, and manipulating the destiny of the one man who can oppose him, will have to train the next heir of Cassandra to take her place before his Coming.<br /><br />However, with the years to have taken him from city to city, and from battle to battle, making him well-known across Greece and Asia Minor alike as a great strategist beyond compare, when his destiny leads him back to Macedonia, and the followers of the Dark God set in motion their final plans that will pave the way for his Coming, Parmenion will find himself facing the forces of Darkness, holding in his hands the soul of an innocent unborn child who, if he fails to restore it, could mean the beginning of the end of the world as they knew it.<br /><br />With a deep and rich history like the Greek one, having drawn the attention through the millennia of myriad scholars, philosophers, historians and archaeologists, bringing to light legends and heroes from the distant past, David Gemmell – choosing one of the most classical periods of ancient Greece: the 4th century BC – immerses us in the <i>Lion of Macedon</i> to the city of Sparta, which, with its society to live under its own rules, putting the young boys from the age of seven to be trained through a rigorous program until their manhood in their twentieth years to serve as warriors, but also giving to women the freedom to exercise equally among the men so that they can deliver strong children, has become the greatest military might in Greece after the fleeing of the Persians, and the fear of their enemies.<br />As well as to Macedonia, which, surrounded by Illyrians, Thracians, Paionians and Thebans, forced to fight one war after the other that have given rise to intrigues and power-struggles for the throne, and decimated the land and its people, has suffered more than any other city in Greece – a divided nation that, with every city-state seeking to rise to power and to spread its own dominance, reveals a quite different Greece from today's.<br /><br />A novel in which, based on the great historical events that took place in Cadmea, Leuctra and Heraclea Lyncestis, Gemmell revives this classical period, reshaping the world of ancient Greece to his imagination, and traveling us in an epic story of warriors, generals, kings, priestesses and creatures of the underworld, using multiple characters and points of view that extends it far more – but always keeping his main protagonist at the center of his narrative – and creating a sweeping adventure full of battles and wars, intrigues and plots, great love affairs and hated enemies, that shows the greatness of his writing.<br /><br />In short, <i>Lion of Macedon</i> is a great first half of the Greek series, with David Gemmell to immerses us into one of the most classical periods of ancient Greece, and traveling us in a story of generals, kings and priestesses, but also in an adventure of love, glory and war that creates through his imagination an epic and magical historical fantasy novel.<br /><br />Ελληνική κριτική:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Πίσω στις αρχές της δεκαετίας του ‘90, όταν η καριέρα του ακόμη μεγάλωνε τότε, ο David Gemmell, παίρνοντας ένα ταξίδι στην Λίνδο, στο νησί της Ρόδου, και μια εμπειρία που αποδείχθηκε πιο εμπνεόμενη απ’ ότι θα περίμενε, άρχισε να χτίζει τις πρώτες ιδέες του για την επόμενη ιστορία του, φέρνοντας στη ζωή ξανά από τα βάθη της ελληνικής ιστορίας έναν μακρά ξεχασμένο θρύλο: τον Παρμενίων.<br />Και στο <i>Lion of Macedon</i>, το πρώτο από τα δύο μέρη της Ελληνικής σειράς, ο Gemmell, βασισμένος στα αληθινά γεγονότα όπως γράφτηκαν στην ιστορία, δημιουργεί μέσα από την φαντασία του τον δικό του κόσμο των αρχαίων χρόνων, ταξιδεύοντάς μας σε μια ιστορία μισθοφόρων και στρατηγών, φιλοσόφων και ρητόρων, και μαντισσών και ιερισσών, αλλά και σε μια περιπέτεια αγάπης και δόξας, εκδίκησης και πολέμου, και πεπρωμένου και μαγείας, σε ένα επικό, ιστορικής φαντασίας μυθιστόρημα.<br /><br />Για σχεδόν έναν αιώνα από την μεγάλη εισβολή του Ξέρξη, όταν ο θρυλικός Βασιλεύς του Σπαθιού Λεωνίδας και οι τριακόσιοι άνδρες του στάθηκαν στο Πέρασμα των Θερμοπυλών, και όταν όχι πολύ αργότερα πέντε χιλιάδες ενωμένοι Σπαρτιάτες συνάντησαν τον Περσικό στρατό αναγκάζοντάς τον να τραπεί σε φυγή από τα εδάφη τους, η Σπάρτη, ένα μέρος απ’ όπου ήρωες και μεγάλοι πολεμιστές γεννιούνται, έχει γίνει η πιο στρατιωτικά ισχυρή και ένδοξη πόλη, εξαπλώνοντας την κυριαρχία της σε όλη την Ελλάδα – αλλά ο Παρμενίων, έχοντας παρθεί από την Μακεδονική μητέρα στην ηλικία των έβδομων χρόνων του για να εκπαιδευτεί στους τρόπους των πολεμιστών, πέφτοντας θύμα των εμπαιγμών και χλευασμών των άλλων παιδιών για την ημίαιμη καταγωγή του, ονειρεύεται όλη την νεαρή ζωή του για την μέρα που θα νιώσει τη δόξα της νίκης στο πλευρό του Βασιλιά. <br />Θέλοντας να αποδειχθεί άξιος για την πλευρά του πατέρα του, και να κάνει περήφανη την μητέρα του για τις θυσίες που υπέστη για να τον μεγαλώσει μετά τον θάνατό του, ελπίζοντας να της φέρει λίγη χαρά, ο Παρμενίων εξασκείται σκληρά μέρα με την μέρα, ξεπερνώντας τους αντίπαλούς του στους διαγωνισμούς τρεξίματος, και φέρνοντάς τον πιο κοντά από οποιονδήποτε άλλον του στρατώνα του στον Τελικό των Παιχνιδιών του Στρατηγού και στο μεγαλύτερο έπαθλο που θα μπορούσε να έχει οποιοσδήποτε Σπαρτιάτης: ένα από τα εφτά σπαθιά του Λεωνίδα του Βασιλέα.<br />Κι όμως, με την ημίαιμη καταγωγή του να έχει προκαλέσει την ένσταση του Βασιλιά Αγησίλαου στο να διαγωνιστεί στον Τελικό, χειραγωγώντας τους κριτές υπέρ του ανιψιού του, όταν οι προσεκτικά προετοιμασμένες στρατηγικές του οδηγήσουν σε ένα συντριπτικό αποτέλεσμα όπως κανένας άλλος δεν έχει επιτύχει ποτέ ξανά, και ερωτευτεί ένα κορίτσι που είχε υποσχεθεί για κάποιον άλλον, ο Παρμενίων θα βρεθεί σύντομα στον στόχο των ευγενών οικογενειών, αναζητώντας αποκατάσταση για την ντροπή και την ταπείνωση που τους έφερε, και βάζοντάς τον σε ένα μονοπάτι που θα του στερήσει όλα όσα αγάπησε και νοιάστηκε σε αυτή την πόλη.<br /><br />Εν τω μεταξύ, στην Θήβα, ο Επαμεινώνδας, έχοντας νιώσει το βάρος της σπαρτιατικής ηγεμονίας μετά την κατοχή της Καδμείας από τα στρατεύματά τους, βλέποντας τον λαό του να πέφτει σε καθημερινά βάσανα, δολοπλοκεί και σχεδιάζει από τότε μαζί με τον Καλέπιο και τον Πελοπίδα, αναζητώντας για έναν τρόπο που θα ελευθερώσει την πόλη που μεγάλωσαν και αγάπησαν· ο Φίλιππος, έχοντας δοθεί σαν όμηρος μετά την δολοφονία του πατέρα του, και την αρπαγή του θρόνου από τον θείο του, Πτολεμαίο, περιμένει για την μέρα που αυτός και ο αδερφός του, Περδίκκας, θα πάρουν πίσω την Μακεδονία και την κληρονομιά τους και θα την φέρουν ξανά στη δόξα· ενώ η Τάμις, έχοντας περπατήσει τα μονοπάτια του παρελθόντος και του μέλλοντος, βλέποντας την γέννηση του Σκοτεινού Θεού, και χειραγωγώντας το πεπρωμένο του ενός άνδρα που μπορεί να του αντισταθεί, θα πρέπει να εκπαιδεύσει την επόμενη κληρονόμο της Κασσάνδρας για να πάρει την θέση της πριν τον Ερχομό του.<br /><br />Ωστόσο, με τα χρόνια να τον έχουν πάρει από πόλη σε πόλη, και από μάχη σε μάχη, κάνοντάς τον ξακουστό σε όλη την Ελλάδα και την Μικρά Ασία ομοίως ως έναν σπουδαίο σχεδιαστή στρατηγικών πέραν σύγκρισης, όταν το πεπρωμένο του τον οδηγήσει πίσω στην Μακεδονία, και οι ακόλουθοι του Σκοτεινού Θεού θέσουν σε κίνηση τα τελικά σχέδιά τους που θα ανοίξουν το δρόμο για τον Ερχομό του, ο Παρμενίων θα βρεθεί να αντιμετωπίζει τις δυνάμεις του Σκότους, κρατώντας στα χέρια του την ψυχή ενός αθώου αγέννητου παιδιού που, αν αποτύχει να την επαναφέρει, θα μπορούσε να σημάνει το ξεκίνημα του τέλους του κόσμου όπως τον ξέρανε.<br /><br />Με μια βαθιά και πλούσια ιστορία όπως αυτή της ελληνικής, έχοντας τραβήξει την προσοχή μέσα από τις χιλιετίες μυριάδων μελετητών, φιλοσόφων, ιστορικών και αρχαιολόγων, φέρνοντας στο φως θρύλους και ήρωες από το μακρινό παρελθόν, ο David Gemmell - επιλέγοντας μια από τις πιο κλασικές περιόδους της αρχαίας Ελλάδας: τον 4ο αιώνα π.Χ. - μας βυθίζει στο <i>Lion of Macedon</i> στην πόλη της Σπάρτης, η οποία, με την κοινωνία της να ζει κάτω από τους δικούς της κανόνες, βάζοντας τα νεαρά αγόρια από την ηλικία των εφτά να εκπαιδευτούν μέσω ενός αυστηρού πρόγραμμα μέχρι την ενηλικίωσή τους σε άνδρες στα είκοσί τους χρόνια για να υπηρετήσουν ως πολεμιστές, αλλά και δίνοντας και στις γυναίκες την ελευθερία να εξασκούνται ισάξια ανάμεσα στους άνδρες ώστε να μπορούν να παραδώσουν γερά παιδιά, έχει γίνει η μεγαλύτερη στρατιωτική ισχύ στην Ελλάδα μετά την φυγή των Περσών, και ο φόβος των εχθρών τους.<br />Όπως επίσης και στην Μακεδονία, η οποία, περικυκλωμένη από Ιλλυριούς, Θράκες, Παίονες και Θηβαίους, αναγκασμένοι να πολεμάνε τον έναν πόλεμο μετά τον άλλον που έχουν προκαλέσει ίντριγκες και πάλες για την εξουσία για τον θρόνο, και αποδεκατίσει την γη και τον λαό της, έχει υποφέρει περισσότερο από οποιαδήποτε άλλη πόλη της Ελλάδας – ένα διχασμένο έθνος που, με την κάθε πόλη-πολιτεία να αναζητεί να εγερθεί στην εξουσία και να εξαπλώσει την δικιά της κυριαρχία της, αποκαλύπτει μια αρκετά διαφορετική Ελλάδα από του σήμερα.<br /><br />Ένα μυθιστόρημα στο οποίο, βασιζόμενος στα σπουδαία ιστορικά γεγονότα που πήραν μέρος στην Καδμεία, την Λεύκτρα και την Ηράκλεια Λυγκηστίς, ο Gemmell ξαναζωντανεύει αυτή την κλασική εποχή, αναδιαμορφώνοντας τον κόσμο της αρχαίας Ελλάδας στην φαντασία του, και ταξιδεύοντάς μας σε μια επική ιστορία πολεμιστών, στρατηγών, βασιλιάδων, ιερισσών και πλασμάτων του κάτω κόσμου, χρησιμοποιώντας πολλαπλούς χαρακτήρες και οπτικές γωνίες που την επεκτείνει πολύ περισσότερο – αλλά κρατώντας πάντα τον κύριο πρωταγωνιστή του στο κέντρο της αφήγησής του – και δημιουργώντας μια σαρωτική περιπέτεια γεμάτη μάχες και πολέμους, ίντριγκες και δολοπλοκίες, μεγάλους έρωτες και μισητούς εχθρούς, που δείχνει το μεγαλείο της γραφής του.<br /><br />Εν συντομία, το <i>Lion of Macedon</i> είναι ένα σπουδαίο πρώτο μισό της Ελληνικής σειράς, με τον David Gemmell να μας βυθίζει μέσα σε μια από τις πιο κλασικές περιόδους της αρχαίας Ελλάδας, και ταξιδεύοντάς σε μια ιστορία στρατηγών, βασιλιάδων και ιερισσών, αλλά και σε μια περιπέτεια αγάπης, δόξας και πολέμου που δημιουργεί μέσα από την φαντασία του ένα επικό και μαγικό μυθιστόρημα ιστορικής φαντασίας. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="17461136774348902090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1691294823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1691294823" />
    <a title="Thomas R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40997266-thomas-r"><img alt="Thomas R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483234941p2/40997266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1691294823?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas R." href="/user/show/40997266-thomas-r">Thomas R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1691294823&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1691294823" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9549751724523004059">Wow! What an incredible story!<br/><br/>I have much love for Greek history, especially for Spartans. And the first thing I liked about this book was the rich culture, history and clear research which had gone into the story. <br/><br/>Parmenion, a young boy training to be a Spartan soldier but robbed of his childhood as those around him plot to humiliate, ridicule and even try to kill him. This sets the setting for his life as he becomes angry and vengeful which, brings about the fall of Sparta.<br/><br/>The book is written </span>
  <span id="freeText9549751724523004059" style="display:none">Wow! What an incredible story!<br /><br />I have much love for Greek history, especially for Spartans. And the first thing I liked about this book was the rich culture, history and clear research which had gone into the story. <br /><br />Parmenion, a young boy training to be a Spartan soldier but robbed of his childhood as those around him plot to humiliate, ridicule and even try to kill him. This sets the setting for his life as he becomes angry and vengeful which, brings about the fall of Sparta.<br /><br />The book is written very well. I was kept interested throughout and everything fell into place. It's not just a historical book but had a fantasy feel throughout (especially at the end!) with magus's, witches and gods. I also noticed that Gemmell likes his characters to have out of body experiences as they fly and saw across the sky (like The King Beyond the Gate and Waylander).<br /><br />The ending surprised me as the time changes as Parmenion and Aristotle brace the underworld. And when the 300 came along I was like WHOA!!! Great moment it was :-)<br /><br />I did think that the Spartan training did not come across as brutal as I have read it to be. It was as an almost daily test of pain but I got the impression it was just Parmenion turning up at the agora to practice duelling days on end.<br /><br />Also, the blurb says that "Despised by Spartan's and Macedonians alike." Now I've finished I can see now why the Spartans hate him but not the Macedonians (there is a secret yet to be revealed to them I guess), this may come about in book II however, I felt that this should not have been in the blurb as the Macedonias come to victory by the end, put their place on the map and was good friends with the King, so, not sure why that was there but anywho, this book really is fantastic.<br /><br />I'm keen to read more of Gemmell's historical fantasy and this gets a full 5 stars from me.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9549751724523004059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710057748" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10332506302312385704">I don't know how I missed this particular of book and am so glad I was made aware of its existence. It rivals the Rigante series in terms of it's protagonist and covers a fantastic period of history that contains some of the most epic battles of all time.<br/><br/>Parmenion is a man without a people. Born to a Macedonian mother he is treated as a second class citizen in his homeland of Sparta despite possessing the very qualities that made Sparta what it is. He is cunning and driven and spends much of his</span>
  <span id="freeText10332506302312385704" style="display:none">I don't know how I missed this particular of book and am so glad I was made aware of its existence. It rivals the Rigante series in terms of it's protagonist and covers a fantastic period of history that contains some of the most epic battles of all time.<br /><br />Parmenion is a man without a people. Born to a Macedonian mother he is treated as a second class citizen in his homeland of Sparta despite possessing the very qualities that made Sparta what it is. He is cunning and driven and spends much of his life being manipulated by a mage who has seen a thousand terrible futures and intends him to be her soldier against the darkness.<br /><br />The question of why Greece never united and become to world power it could have been is an interesting one. The idea that every army has Greek mercenaries, as they are the best fighting soldiers, but that the armies of Greece herself are fractured and hamstrung by infighting and ambition intrigued me. If only they had gotten their shit together!<br /><br />The ending is amazing. I thought I knew where things were going but the amount of backflips and 180's in the finale really tuned things on its head and made me look forward to the second book even more so. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10332506302312385704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_722838233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722838233" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7177008-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388366904p2/7177008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722838233?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/7177008-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099703501" href="/book/show/1262454.Lion_of_Macedon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=ancient-greece">ancient-greece</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7177008-jane?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722838233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1195162350707648187">This historical fantasy really captured my interest from the first page and held it all through. This is the story of the life of the ancient Greek general, Parmenion, from boyhood in Sparta where he has always been regarded as a misfit because of his mixed Spartan/Macedonian parentage and treated cruelly and unfairly. General Xenophon [THAT Xenophon of the <i> Anabasis </i>] takes him under his wing and mentors him. When the boy reaches manhood, he leaves Sparta with vengeance in his heart and as a me</span>
  <span id="freeText1195162350707648187" style="display:none">This historical fantasy really captured my interest from the first page and held it all through. This is the story of the life of the ancient Greek general, Parmenion, from boyhood in Sparta where he has always been regarded as a misfit because of his mixed Spartan/Macedonian parentage and treated cruelly and unfairly. General Xenophon [THAT Xenophon of the <i> Anabasis </i>] takes him under his wing and mentors him. When the boy reaches manhood, he leaves Sparta with vengeance in his heart and as a mercenary soldier is instrumental in the victory of Thebes over Sparta at Leuctra and beyond, finally breaking Sparta's power. Then he travels as a mercenary to Persia, finally travelling to Macedonia, where he, now promoted to General, forms an army for Philip II. Unbeknownst to him, a sorceress has been controlling his life, as well as that of his lost love, Denae, hoping to defeat the powers of Darkness. The ending packed a wallop!<br /><br />The first part set in Sparta was cliché-ridden: the underdog mistreated at the hands of others; the sick mother; the one loyal friend; the wise mentor. I thought the YA trilogy "Spartan Warrior" did those aspects better. But once Parmenion left Sparta and went to other places, the story took off. We don't know much about Parmenion's early life, so I'm pretty sure the author made everything up until we find him in Macedonia. The facts that in Thebes he trains the Sacred Band and that he devises the winning strategy at Leuctra served only to show his talent and astuteness in military matters. I doubt he was even there in real life. The author built his story on the bare outlines of the history of that period. Parmenion also trains an army for Philip; I enjoyed that section the most. The fantasy was worked in well. The whole book was well-written.<br /><br />Highly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1195162350707648187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10147284052653639215">A book I was thinking about buying for some years...Read it at last and, boy, it was worth it!<br/><br/>Well, I'll give it a five though it's not a straight 10/10 cause I loved it.   <span id="freeText10147284052653639215" style="display:none">A book I was thinking about buying for some years...Read it at last and, boy, it was worth it!<br /><br />Well, I'll give it a five though it's not a straight 10/10 cause I loved it. What's not to love? Ancient Greece and fantasy. Sparta, Macedon, Law and Chaos, you name it. Parmenion as a Spartan warrior seemed a bit odd, I don't remember this having any historical background. Also some historical inaccuracies here and there maybe but not too many. Actually too *few*! This first part that has little fantasy is one of the most accurate fiction for ancient Greece that I have read, coming to think of it. I liked Parmenion as a character. Great guy but he had his flaws. The rest of the cast are nicely done too. Weird thing is I didn't like Gemmell's epic fantasy that much but he's pretty good in fantasy&amp;history blend.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2216074108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2216074108" />
    <a title="The Idle Woman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17228936-the-idle-woman"><img alt="The Idle Woman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465065947p2/17228936.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2216074108?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Idle Woman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Idle Woman" href="/user/show/17228936-the-idle-woman">The Idle Woman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12987204-lion-of-macedon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2216074108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11998630060146126334">Gemmell takes as his hero the young Parmenion, half-Spartan and half-Macedonian, who has grown up with the taunts of his fully Spartan peers. Having failed to impress them with his abilities as an athlete, Parmenion hopes instead to make an impression with his strategic intelligence. Facing up against the popular Leonidas (not that Leonidas), as rival generals in a mock battle, he demonstrates a brilliant tactical broadside that goes against all the rules of Spartan combat, leaving his enemy dec</span>
  <span id="freeText11998630060146126334" style="display:none">Gemmell takes as his hero the young Parmenion, half-Spartan and half-Macedonian, who has grown up with the taunts of his fully Spartan peers. Having failed to impress them with his abilities as an athlete, Parmenion hopes instead to make an impression with his strategic intelligence. Facing up against the popular Leonidas (not that Leonidas), as rival generals in a mock battle, he demonstrates a brilliant tactical broadside that goes against all the rules of Spartan combat, leaving his enemy decimated. The judges are shocked; Leonidas’ cronies are disgusted. But one man in the audience is impressed. That is the Athenian exile Xenophon (yes, that Xenophon), who takes Parmenion under his wing and begins to nurture this nascent strategos‘s gift for warfare. Time passes, and Parmenion realises that the Spartans will never allow a half-blood to rise to the officer class in their army. His life looks set to be spent in the rank-and-file, fighting another man’s battles. But he hasn’t realised that he has a role to play in another war...<br /><br />For the rest of the review, please see my blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theidlewoman.net/2017/12/03/lion-of-macedon-david-gemmell/#more-50724">https://theidlewoman.net/2017/12/03/l...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11998630060146126334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781857236224" href="/book/show/1061687.Lion_of_Macedon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52608370-rebecca?shelf=library-borrowings">library-borrowings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52608370-rebecca?shelf=non-tolkien-fantasy-magic">non-tolkien-fantasy-magic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2109396782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12426863086149398652">I'd heard quite a bit about David Gemmell's novels from other people so thought I'd give them a try. What interested me about this one was that it's based around a fairly well-known era of ancient history, but Gemmell uses the Greek belief in oracles, gods etc as a way of weaving fantasy elements into the story. We focus mainly on a character Parmenion, who Gemmell's introduction describes as "forgotten", but more recognisable figures are threaded into the story as well. <br/><br/>On the downside, this do</span>
  <span id="freeText12426863086149398652" style="display:none">I'd heard quite a bit about David Gemmell's novels from other people so thought I'd give them a try. What interested me about this one was that it's based around a fairly well-known era of ancient history, but Gemmell uses the Greek belief in oracles, gods etc as a way of weaving fantasy elements into the story. We focus mainly on a character Parmenion, who Gemmell's introduction describes as "forgotten", but more recognisable figures are threaded into the story as well. <br /><br />On the downside, this does make things a bit predictable - if you know your ancient history, then it's fairly obvious whose birth the seers are worried about. Equally, that whole plotline about the seers trying to change things allows for the exploration of questions about whether anything *can* be changed. And how does anyone know if the seers have interpreted their visions correctly? It's one thing having power, but using it well... <br /><br />Overall, it's an engrossing read and I will hopefully find the second one soon enough. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12426863086149398652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1074169552350691185">This was my first novel by David Gemmell. I thought I will start with a lesser known book and leave the better ones for later. Well, I was wrong to assume that I will get a weaker book, it was a fascinating read.   <span id="freeText1074169552350691185" style="display:none">This was my first novel by David Gemmell. I thought I will start with a lesser known book and leave the better ones for later. Well, I was wrong to assume that I will get a weaker book, it was a fascinating read. Parmenion was a great character and I really liked how more and more character got the spotlight as the scope of event changed. The atmosphere was nice as well I really felt like I was there with the heroes. I also liked the use of magic, it was really fitting to the overall theme. And I do not even have to talk about the battle scenes which are one of the strongest points of this writer. So yes, I can recommend this book to anyone and I am curious how the second story will go.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tVLwgKhzIajwiY0T+DRd+opUePA9WGUlqs41fPgXQCiX9aB78+iUG0NGW/WeJZ53b1XeyLT8sMhjExP3L8ea9w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yaICkPdoYi99tXWxILSyUxP/Qgqmv/GtnOxjKcz2w1TrBVJrrPPXnM56o1dGpXHe9v7kMi8bJEBVMUWiGyYZiw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer9777167619033898520">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sel</span>
  <span id="freeText9777167619033898520" style="display:none">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sell worldwide.</span>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script>
